Ministry of Finance Approves Issuance of Tax-Exempt Transportation Permits for Homespun Cloth

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce previously sent a telegram to the Ministry of Finance, requesting that the competent authorities be instructed to issue tax-exempt transportation permits for the transportation of handmade homespun cloth, and to inform the customs to verify and release the goods. Now, it is learned that the chamber received a reply from the ministry yesterday, stating: "The telegram has been received. The case submitted by the National Taxation Administration has been examined. It is found that this case was previously submitted to the administration by the Shanghai Yarn and Cloth Association and the Homespun Cloth Industry Association. The administration deemed that handmade homespun cloth, if made of cotton yarn on which national taxes have been paid, should be exempt from national taxes. However, for homespun cloth made of cotton yarn purchased in small quantities, the original tax receipts for the cotton yarn cannot be obtained, so it cannot be proved that taxes have been paid. In order to give special consideration to the difficulties of merchants, it is tentatively allowed that after the expiration of the period for exempting cotton yarn and its direct woven products from national taxes, they can apply for transportation permits in the same way as direct woven products holding the original cotton yarn tax receipts, so that the customs can verify and release the goods." The reply was sent to the association for information and instructed the Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui National Taxation Bureau to comply. This order is hereby issued for your information.

Surtax on Deed Tax for Local Autonomy Expenses

The Shanghai County Government, due to the shortage of local autonomy funds in the county, had previously proposed and resolved at the county administrative meeting to levy a surtax on deed taxes and other items to supplement the funds. The county government then submitted a formal document to the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Finance for approval. The Department of Finance replied, stating that since the surtax on deed taxes in the county is not much, the request to follow the example of special construction donations and levy one yuan per hundred yuan of the sale deed price and five jiao per hundred yuan of the pawn deed price is tentatively approved. Therefore, the county finance bureau received an order from the county government yesterday, instructing that the surtax be levied according to the plan from this year onwards and allocated for local autonomy expenses.

Slaughter Tax to be Collected as Usual

The Shanghai County Government issued an announcement yesterday, stating: "In accordance with the instruction from the Jiangsu Education Funding Management Office, it is hereby announced that before the office approves someone to take over the Shanghai slaughter tax, the tax payments for March and April should still be collected by the original committee member Fan Chunqiu as usual. Furthermore, Committee Member Fan stated in his letter that the slaughter tax for March and April has been ordered by the Jiangsu Education Funding Management Office to be collected as usual, and there are also previous arrears. Please issue an announcement quickly and strictly supervise the collection so that the funds can be collected and remitted. Approved. Therefore, this announcement is issued. All households and individuals who are recognized as paying the slaughter tax must comply. It should be known that the slaughter tax is still being collected as usual. All previous arrears and taxes due for March and April must be paid quickly. Do not delay or wait and see, or you will be subject to prosecution. Each should respectfully comply without violation. Sincerely."

Relaxation of Restrictions on Housing in the Chinese Area

▲ Suspension of Crackdown on Residents with No Public Safety Issues

Since Zhu Xiaoyun submitted a report to the Municipal Government in the 18th year of the Republic of China, requesting the crackdown on second landlords who abused renting and overcrowding, which hindered hygiene, the Public Security Bureau, Public Works Bureau, and Health Bureau implemented measures to restrict the subletting of housing for civilians: (1) no more than three households in a single building; (2) no more than five households in a double building; (3) no more than six households in a triple building; (4) sun decks and kitchens shall not be converted into dwellings; (5) no mezzanine floors shall be added without the permission of the Public Works Bureau. Although these measures were approved by the Municipal Government, they have not been effectively implemented. In March of this year, the Fourth District Executive Committee of the Municipal Party Department again urged the Public Security Bureau to strictly implement the measures. As a result, the residents of the Chinese area complained that the Public Security Bureau did not care about the people's livelihood, and they did not know that the proposer of this case was someone else, and the Public Security Bureau was only the executor. It is now heard that the Public Security Bureau feels that the implementation is difficult and has a great impact on the livelihoods of civilians. It has discussed the matter with the Municipal Party Department again and again. As a result, a flexible approach has been adopted. The content is that the existing households rented before will be temporarily exempted from the crackdown if there are no public safety issues. If the original residents move out, the second landlord shall not recruit other households. Strict crackdown will be enforced only if they deliberately violate the rules. After receiving the order, each district has temporarily suspended the implementation of this case. Therefore, the issue of restricting housing in the Chinese area has come to an end.

Summary of the National Calendar for the 21st Year of the Republic of China

▲ Can be Requested from the Fourth Section of the Social Affairs Bureau by Letter

The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, in order to provide a basis for civilian-printed calendars, diaries, monthly calendars, and other books for the 21st year, reprinted twenty copies of the calendar summary compiled by the Astronomical Research Institute of the Academia Sinica, which were issued by the Ministry of Interior and the Ministry of Education. Previously, it was announced that the publishing and printing industries could claim them. In recent days, many bookstores in this city and other provinces have come to request them. Now, because there are still some remaining, those in need in this city bureau are allowed to request them by letter. Please include a self-addressed stamped envelope with the name and address of the requester, and they will be sent.

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Urges Payment of Membership Fees

▲ Otherwise, the Rights Enjoyed by Members Will Be Suspended

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce sent letters yesterday to the members of the Securities, Cured Meat, Rice Grain Sales, Seafood, Hardware, Embroidery Printing, Clothing, and other trade associations, as well as the Changfeng, Yili, Zhenhua, Jiangnan, Yizhong, Huacheng, and other shop members, stating: "Article 31 of the Chamber of Commerce Law promulgated by the National Government stipulates that the expenses of the chamber of commerce are divided into the following two types: First, administrative expenses, which are borne by the members in proportion to the number of representatives they send and the amount of capital. Now, the annual membership fee to be collected from each member depends on the amount of operating capital reported. Therefore, if the amount of capital fluctuates one day, the membership fee cannot be determined. Before the general meeting of members on June 21 of last year, although the members of each association and the shop members had paid some attendance fees, the standard for charging fees according to capital had not been decided by the general meeting of members, so it was impossible to determine the amount of fees. Therefore, the calculation was temporarily based on the number of people, with each association paying 50 yuan for each representative sent, and each shop paying 30 yuan for each representative sent. The amount of the shortfall was announced at that time, and it was stated that it would be made up after all the capital amounts were reported. In other words, the previously paid attendance fee is part of the membership fee for the 19th year. If any member has paid the attendance fee and believes that the membership fee has been paid in full, it is a fundamental error. This chamber has issued announcements repeatedly based on the above reasons to urge the reporting of capital with record. Now, it has been found that a small number of members have reported their capital but have not paid the membership fees that should be made up, and some have not even reported their capital. This is a lack of obligation that members should fulfill. Therefore, this letter is sent again to inform you that you must report the capital amount to the association within one week of receiving this letter, so that we can make up the membership fee. Those who have reported their capital but have not paid the fees that should be made up must also make up the fees within one week of receiving this letter. Otherwise, we will have to temporarily suspend the rights enjoyed by members in accordance with Article 22 of the charter of this association.

Commander Deng Inspects the Wusong Fort

▲Protecting the Fishing Season

After receiving instructions from the Ministry of Military Administration and issuing the newly compiled table of organization for the fortress, Deng Zhenquan, the commander of the Wusong Fortress, immediately began the reorganization, eliminating the old and weak, reorganizing various aspects, and reissuing new circular badges. At 9:00 AM yesterday, he gathered all officers in the department for a memorial week event. Then, accompanied by the Chief of Staff, Deputy Chief Adjutant Shen, several adjutants, he proceeded to the North and South forts and the Lion Grove Fort to inspect the large and small gun emplacements and review the artillery drills. In the afternoon, he continued to explore the lighthouse garrison campfires and other areas, conducting a tour for a week before returning to the department. It is reported that Commander Deng has strictly protected the spring fishing season at Wusong, as it is related to national tax revenue. He ordered his subordinates to pay attention to suspicious vessels to prevent bandits from infiltrating, and strictly prohibited tourists from secretly taking photographs of the fort. Violators, regardless of Chinese or foreign individuals, will be detained and dealt with.

County Party Reorganization Committee Implements Work Plan

▲The First Phase of Work is Completed

The Jiangsu Provincial Party Reorganization Committee formulated a temporary work implementation plan at the beginning of the 20th year and issued it to various counties for implementation. Shanghai County began work on January 13th. The first step was to conduct surveys of party members and society. The committee first studied survey methods, divided survey areas and personnel. From January 16th, committee members Lü Zhe, Tao Yishan, and Jiang Yanqiu, along with staff, conducted surveys in different areas every day. By February 8th, using open, secret, direct, indirect, and various other methods, and in accordance with various survey forms issued by the province, they had meticulously surveyed all party members in the county, as well as all organs, groups, schools, factories, special local conditions, and local figures, compiling various statistics to be submitted to the province. The second step was to re-divide the six district party branches and twenty-seven sub-district party branches into four district party branches, fourteen sub-district party branches, and two directly affiliated sub-district branches, based on the province's district division principles, the information obtained from this survey, traffic conditions, special local conditions, population size, and the ratio of party members, in consultation with provincial instructors. They also defined the activity scope of each district party branch and sub-district party branch, designated activity areas and targets for each party member, and assigned current activities. At this point, the first phase of the temporary work implementation plan issued by the province was completed. The committee, together with the provincial instructor, reported to the Party Reorganization Committee and received instructions stating that the work was diligent, the results were quite good, and it was commendable. It is also reported that all district and sub-district party branches in the county, by the 10th of this month, have been personally guided by three reorganization committee members to establish themselves one after another.

Reorganization of the Defense Corps Completed

▲The Municipal Government Appoints Members to the Management Committee

The defense corps in various districts of this city, since October of the 18th year, after the municipal government appointed Councilor Sun Baorong, gentry and business leaders Yao Mulian, Ye Huijun, Wang Xiaolai, and others to organize a reorganization committee to engage in reorganization, the committee has already reported the completion of the reorganization. Now, the municipal government has ordered the dissolution of the committee and separately appointed Sun Baorong, Luo Jingyou, and others as members of the management committee of the city's defense corps, establishing a new management committee. The list of members and the organizational rules of the management committee are recorded below.

▲List of Members: Sun Baorong, Luo Jingyou, Chen Xizeng, Yu Hede, Ye Huijun, Ni Mulian, Wang Xiaolai, Wang Yansong, Wang Dong, nine people. Among them, except for Luo Jingyou who is newly appointed, the rest are all members of the previous reorganization committee. Mr. Luo is the section chief of the Second Section of the Municipal Government, a graduate of the Army University, and formerly served as the chief of staff of the Anhui National Army, a counselor of the General Headquarters of the National Revolutionary Army, and a senior staff officer of the Military Affairs Commission of the National Government. He is currently the section chief of the Second Section of the Municipal Government.

▲Organizational Rules: "Organizational Rules of the Shanghai Municipal Defense Corps Management Committee" Article 1: This committee (hereinafter referred to as "the committee") is organized by personnel dispatched by the municipal government. Article 2: The committee, under the orders of the municipal government, is responsible for the management of the city's defense corps. Article 3: The functions of the committee are as follows: (1) Matters concerning the organization, training, command, and dispatch of the city's defense corps; (2) Matters concerning the promotion, transfer, recruitment, awards, and punishments of officers and personnel of the city's defense corps; (3) Matters concerning the maintenance and rectification of discipline of the corps; (4) Other matters that should be managed. Article 4: The committee shall consist of nine members, who shall mutually elect three members as standing committee members and report to the municipal government for approval and record. Article 5: The committee shall hold meetings twice a month, and temporary meetings may be convened by the standing committee members when necessary. The detailed rules for the meetings shall be determined separately. Article 6: The standing committee members shall handle daily official duties, and major events shall be discussed and decided upon at meetings. Article 7: The committee may establish one chief instructor, one document clerk, one accountant, two clerks, and three secretaries as needed for business purposes, who shall be appointed or employed separately by the standing committee members. Article 8: The number of staff members of the committee may be increased or decreased at any time as the complexity of affairs requires, subject to reporting. Article 9: The staff members of the committee shall be under the direction and supervision of the standing committee members. Article 10: When it is necessary to establish temporary subsidiary organs for the execution of business, the standing committee members may propose it, and it shall be organized after being approved by the meeting and reported to the municipal government for approval. Article 11: The detailed rules for the committee's work shall be determined separately. Article 12: If there are any matters not covered in these rules, they may be reported for amendment at any time. Article 13: These rules shall be implemented from the date of promulgation with the approval of the municipal government.

Detailed Rules for the Implementation of the Labor-Capital Dispute Resolution Law

▲Approved by the National Government and Promulgated for Implementation After Being Submitted by the Municipal Government

The detailed rules for the implementation of the labor-capital dispute resolution law in this city have now been approved by the National Government after being submitted by the municipal government. They were announced by the municipal government yesterday and forwarded to the Social Affairs Bureau for compliance and implementation. The original text is as follows: (Article 1) These detailed rules are formulated by the Shanghai Municipal Government in accordance with the provisions of Article 39 of the Labor-Capital Dispute Resolution Law (hereinafter referred to as "the Law"). (Article 2) The competent administrative organ to which labor-capital dispute cases in this city are affiliated shall be the Social Affairs Bureau under the Municipal Government Bureau for mediation and the Municipal Government for arbitration. (Article 3) If a dispute occurs in the special district of this city, the arbitration committee member of Article 13, Item 3 of this Law shall be filled by a representative appointed by the local court of the special district. (Article 4) The representative of Article 13, Item 4 of this Law and the representative designated on behalf of Article 8 shall not decline after being designated by the competent administrative organ. If it is impossible to assume the position due to a definite accident, a reason shall be stated within three days after receiving the notice, and another appointment shall be made with the approval of the competent administrative organ. (Article 5) The representative appointed by a party shall submit supporting documents when attending the meeting. (Article 6) Neither party may make new demands or conditions after the start of mediation and before the case is resolved. (Article 7) After a labor-capital dispute case has been mediated by the mediation committee or arbitrated by the arbitration committee, the competent administrative organ shall immediately urge the disputing parties to faithfully perform in accordance with the methods stipulated in the mediation record or arbitration award. (Article 8) When a disputing party declares dissent to the arbitration award, it shall file a lawsuit in accordance with the law to the affiliated court within fifteen days from the day following the declaration of dissent. If the lawsuit is not filed after the deadline, it shall still be deemed as not declaring dissent. (Article 9) Contracts or labor agreements between disputing parties shall be deemed valid for at least one year if there is no time limit stipulated. (Article 10) The date of commencement of the mediation or arbitration procedure shall be calculated from the date on which either party applies for mediation or arbitration. When the competent administrative organ submits it for mediation or arbitration, it shall be calculated from the date of notifying the parties. (Article 11) The mediation or arbitration procedure shall end on the date when the mediation committee or arbitration committee delivers the mediation result or arbitration award to both parties. (Article 12) Except for the restrictions on acts stipulated in Articles 33 and 34 of this Law, if the competent administrative organ and the mediation committee or arbitration committee consider that there are other inappropriate acts by the disputing parties, the provisions of Articles 35 and 38 of this Law may be applied mutatis mutandis. (Article 13) The special district local court may assist the disputing parties or witnesses and related industrial and commercial firms, etc., residing in the special district of this city in resisting the orders of the competent administrative organ and the mediation and arbitration institutions, or refusing mediation. (Article 14) These detailed rules shall be implemented from the date of promulgation by this municipal government after being approved by the National Government.

The Municipal Party Headquarters' Stance on the Labor Strikes at Xiehua and Sanxing Factories

▲Sanctions Should Be Imposed for Non-Compliance with Laws and Regulations

▲Assistance Should Be Provided for Losses Suffered

According to the Kuomin News Agency, regarding the recent cases of workers in factories such as Xiehua Silk Weaving Factory and Sanxing Tobacco Factory in this city going on strike on their own, a reporter from the Kuomin News Agency visited Chen Junyi, the standing committee member of the Mass Training Committee of the Municipal Party Headquarters, yesterday to inquire about the facts of each case and the Party Headquarters' attitude towards handling these labor strikes. The following is a record of Mr. Chen's remarks: (The following is the statement of Committee Member Chen) It has been found that the workers of factories such as Xiehua Silk Weaving Factory suddenly went on strike on their own this time, without first going through legal procedures to request the Party and government organs to mediate, and without the approval or permission of this Party Headquarters at the time, which is inappropriate. Because the Party Headquarters protects and cultivates laborers and has the responsibility of guiding them, it will naturally try to increase the welfare of workers. If workers encounter difficulties or are oppressed, the Party Headquarters will give full assistance if they come to request it through legal procedures. Now that the workers of factories such as Xiehua Factory have gone on strike without going through legal procedures and without the approval of the Party Headquarters, they have put themselves in illegal behavior. This Party Headquarters will not only be unable to provide assistance but should also impose sanctions in accordance with discipline. Moreover, the labor strikes in these factories were not organized by the labor unions of the respective factories. I suspect that a few reactionary elements were mixed in and secretly manipulating and inciting the workers. Those who are not restricted by the labor unions and who independently go on strike without being directed or commanded by the labor unions, in addition to the fact that this Party Headquarters has sent personnel to conduct strict investigations, in the future, any workers in various industries who independently go on strike again without going through legal procedures, this Party Headquarters will consult with the government organs in charge to impose severe sanctions and will discuss and formulate measures to strictly punish them and will never be lenient. As for the workers of the French Concession Water and Electricity Factory who suddenly went on strike because of a trivial matter of dumping garbage and a conflict with the police, it was also a fundamental mistake. Because this time it was a personal quarrel between a worker and the police, it was not a labor-capital issue, nor was it the issue of all the workers, and there was absolutely no possibility of involving all the workers, and there was absolutely no need to strike. Such a strike is also illegal. However, since the workers were beaten and injured by the police, the Party Headquarters will, out of consideration for the workers' childish ignorance and lack of understanding, in addition to exempting them from further investigation, definitely negotiate to find a way to compensate for the losses suffered by the workers. If such incidents occur again in the future, severe sanctions will be imposed and there will be absolutely no leniency.

Strike at Three Silk Weaving Factories in Hongkou

▲The Social Affairs Bureau Conducts Mediation

All male and female workers of Xiehua, Yuhua, and Fenghua Silk Weaving Factories on Tangshan Road in Hongkou District went on strike on the afternoon of the 11th due to opposition to the wage cuts at Xiehua and Yuhua Factories. Yesterday, the Social Affairs Bureau sent personnel to persuade them and scheduled mediation for this afternoon. The various situations are recorded below:

▲Reasons for the Strike: The Third Special District Silk Weaving Industry Union demanded that Xiehua and Yuhua Factories restore wages to 3.3 cents per foot, but mediation convened by the Social Affairs Bureau multiple times failed. On the morning of the 11th, a conflict occurred between worker He Agen and the manager of Xiehua Factory. Thereupon, the workers of Xiehua Factory went on strike in the afternoon. Workers from Yuhua and Fenghua Factories immediately joined to express their support, and the union immediately issued a notice stating: "Notice: Since the strike has occurred, all workers should wait quietly for the union to request mediation from the Municipal Party Headquarters and the Social Affairs Bureau. Do not riot to avoid accidents. This is important."

▲Authorities' Persuasion: After receiving the request from the Third District Silk Weaving Industry Union, the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, due to the strike of workers, which is related to social tranquility, immediately sent Zhu Guilin to persuade all workers to resume work first and wait for a legal solution, and scheduled to convene labor and capital parties for mediation at 1:00 PM this afternoon. It is reported that all workers have agreed to enter the factory and resume work this morning.

▲Letter to the Public Works Bureau: The Third Special District Silk Weaving Industry Union sent a letter to the Public Works Bureau of the Public Concession yesterday stating: "To the esteemed Bureau: The workers of our Xiehua Factory have reached a breaking point due to the factory's unreasonable reduction of wages and oppression of the workers. On the morning of the 11th of this month, at around 12:00 noon, the factory actually insulted the workers, which aroused public outrage. We were forced to announce a strike at 1:00 PM that afternoon. Tracing back to the cause, it was actually caused by the factory's severe oppression. Our union has already requested the Municipal Party Headquarters and the Social Affairs Bureau to mediate in accordance with the law. However, during the strike period, we will strictly order the workers of the factory to maintain order and ensure that no accidents occur. Our union will bear full responsibility for the tranquility of the concession. We deeply fear that the Bureau will misunderstand, so we hereby issue this letter to declare and request that your bureau order the patrol room under your jurisdiction not to interfere in order to facilitate the labor movement. We earnestly hope."

Various Industries Request Reduction of Business Tax

▲Paint Industry: The Paint Industry Association, due to the business tax regulations issued by Jiangsu Province, which stipulated 20 per mille for the rosewood industry, submitted an electric request to the Ministry of Finance for approval and amendment, and it was reduced to 10 per mille. However, rosewood, from the time it is transported from production areas such as Siam until it is made into utensils, undergoes tax payment procedures four or five times. If 10 per mille is levied, the burden will inevitably be too heavy, and there is a difficult situation to maintain. The tax amount in Shanghai will soon be announced by the financial authorities. If it follows the tax amount of Jiangsu Province as a blueprint, then our wood industry will be on the verge of bankruptcy. Therefore, Du Gengsheng, Zhang Fukang, Zhou Shanqing, and Ling Youqiao were dispatched to the Municipal Government Finance Bureau and other agencies to appeal and report the situation to various ministries and courts of the central government, requesting relief in accordance with the law and approval to reduce it to 10 per mille as the highest limit. Yesterday, they received Approval No. 2821 from the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, which is recorded as follows: "Shanghai Municipal Paint Industry Association, an electric report, regarding the business tax of 10 per mille levied on the Western-style wood industry and rosewood industry, please review and reduce it. The matter of the electric report entrusting the collection of business tax on the paint and rosewood industry has been stated to have been previously approved by the Ministry of Finance and should be complied with after amendment. You should still submit it directly to the Ministry of Finance for instructions." After receiving the approval, the association has prepared documents to appeal to various ministries and courts of the central government again.

▲Ginseng and Bird's Nest Industry: The Ginseng and Bird's Nest Industry Association submitted a document to the Municipal Government and the Finance Bureau yesterday stating: "A petition for the business tax rate on ginseng and bird's nest to exceed the provisions of the Ministry's regulations, please reduce it to alleviate the difficulties of merchants and maintain business. We secretly belong to the association that previously petitioned for a reduction in the business tax rate, which was not approved by (Your Excellency) (the Municipal Government), which is extremely anxious. Recently, I saw in the newspaper that (the Municipal Finance Bureau) has amended the business tax regulations, levying 2 per mille on Chinese medicine and 10 per mille on ginseng and bird's nest, which is extremely dismaying. I secretly investigate that ginseng and medicine are both things to treat diseases and are of great importance to the lives of the people. They are neither luxury goods nor are they subject to rectification. If 10 per mille is levied, it not only violates the provisions of Article 4 of the outline issued by the Ministry, but also ginseng and medicine are of the same category and are essential medicines for treating diseases. Ancient prescriptions use ginseng extensively, and even the new trend has medicinal pills such as ginseng regeneration. If the tax rate levied on medicinal materials is the same as that on ginseng and bird's nest, it is no different from deliberately discriminating. Taking a step back, if it is considered that ginseng and bird's nest contain foreign goods, then medicinal materials have never been without imported raw materials. Ginseng and bird's nest are essential medicines for treating diseases, saving people is the main purpose, which is even more important than grain, and should not be used in this way. The tax rate should not be increased. Moreover, Article 7 of the Ministry's Regulations on the Implementation of the Business Tax Regulations clearly stipulates that various business taxes, regardless of whether the business is domestic goods or foreign goods, shall be taxed at the same tax rate. Therefore, in terms of reason and law, ginseng and bird's nest should be subject to the same tax rate as Chinese medicine. It is reasonable to submit a document requesting that Your Excellency approve and instruct the Finance Bureau (Your Bureau) to sympathize with the suffering of the ginseng and bird's nest industry and to correct (correct) the business tax rate on ginseng and bird's nest, which should not exceed 2 per mille, which is a virtue. Presented to Zhang, Mayor of Shanghai Municipality, Cai, Director of the Shanghai Municipal Finance Bureau."

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Appeals for Exemption from Withholding Anhui Rice

▲Telegram to the Central Government

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce, regarding the Anhui Provincial Grain Inspection Office's obstruction of rice from leaving the province, believing that it hinders the people's food, sent a telegram to the National Government and the Executive Yuan, stating briefly: "The rice tax in Anhui Province was originally set up for rice and grain leaving the province. Now, due to repeated strict orders from the Central Government, it is impossible to stop collecting taxes, and it has become armed detention of ships, preventing rice and grain from leaving the province. Considering its intention, it is nothing more than to re-trap rice merchants and make them comply. The situation in this regard is probably clear. Wuhu's commerce has always been dominated by the rice market, and rice merchants in various provinces rely entirely on Anhui rice for supply. Now, detaining ships carrying goods will not only affect Wuhu's commercial market, but also cause panic among the people in various provinces that rely on Anhui rice for supply. At this time, when strict orders to cut taxes are repeatedly issued, the Central Government should have the power to balance how to rectify the discipline of various provinces that openly comply but secretly obstruct. Please first telegraph the province to release all the rice ships detained and not to extort them in order to maintain government orders and relieve merchants' difficulties."

French Concession Court Heard Yesterday

The Nikkei Bank Case

▲Ye, Zhao, Zhou, and Chen Deny Being Directors

▲Seizure of Movable Property in Pharmacies and Bathhouses

▲Both Plaintiff and Defendant Sides Argue

▲The Judge Orders a Two-Week Adjournment for Further Hearing

The case of the collapse of Shanghai Nikkei Bank and the Great World Amusement Savings and Deposits was heard for the seventh time yesterday, focusing on the portion concerning the directors of the Gongfa Company. First, the lawyer Lu Shaozong, representing director Ye Shantao, stated that his client had a protest to lodge regarding the position of director of Gongfa Company. Upon investigation, Ye Shantao and the late Huang Chujiu were close friends. When Huang and Ye jointly organized the Nikkei Exchange in the 10th year of the Republic, Ye Shantao suffered significant losses, and Huang Chujiu was deeply apologetic. He promised to compensate Ye. Later, Huang Chujiu gave Ye Shantao shares worth 2,000 yuan. Subsequently, Ye received a call from Huang, stating that director Gao Qingtang was leaving Shanghai due to personal matters and wanted Ye Shantao to take over the position of director. At that time, Ye refused. Later, Huang entrusted Ye as a consultant, paying him a monthly transportation fee of 40 yuan. Later, Ye Shantao sold the 2,000 yuan shares to someone named Ge. From this, it can be seen that Ye Shantao was neither a director nor a shareholder. He requested that the case be dismissed. The plaintiff's lawyer, Dong Yu, rose to rebut, stating that Ye Shantao was indeed a director and shareholder, and there are records to prove it. If Gongfa Company had prospered, Ye Shantao and others would have enjoyed considerable rights. The denial of being a director and shareholder by Ye is strongly opposed by our lawyer, etc. The lawyer Zhou Xiaoan also stated that if Ye Shantao was neither a director nor a shareholder, why would he have a transportation fee, etc. Judge Gong Chengshen announced that the debate on Ye Shantao's denial of being a director and shareholder was concluded and would be decided later. The lawyer representing director Zhao Qinbo stated that his client, Zhao Qinbo, was a friend of the late Huang Chujiu and had helped him in various matters. Therefore, Huang Chujiu paid him a monthly transportation fee of 100 yuan. He was not a director. He requested dismissal. The plaintiff's lawyer, Fei Xizhen, stated that the defendant, Zhao Qinbo, was indeed a director and shareholder, and also a standing committee member. Therefore, the monthly transportation fee was as high as 100 yuan. There are accurate account books to prove it. How can he deny it? The lawyer Yan Luxiang also stated that if Zhao Qinbo was not a director, there would be no reason for him to have a transportation fee. Considering Zhao's status and personality, how could he help others for a long time of four or five years and take a transportation fee? The plaintiff's lawyer, Jiang Yiping, stated that Zhao Qinbo was neither a director nor a shareholder, and relied on Huang Chujiu's friendship to take a monthly transportation fee of 100 yuan. As the saying goes, "no merit, no reward." Huang Chujiu had friendship with Zhao Qinbo before, and there is no reason for him to have intentionally fabricated Zhao's director status on the shareholder register before his death, harming a friend later. There is written evidence, and the opposing party has not submitted any counter-evidence. The defendant cannot shirk his responsibility. He requested that he be ordered to bear unlimited liability. The judge ordered to wait for a ruling. At this point, the two accountants, Pan Zhaobang and Wu Zheng, rose to request that the director case be temporarily suspended in court. Our accountants have a special matter to request. Recently, our accountants received shocking news. Lawyers such as Wu Jingxiong, representing a group of creditors, requested the seizure of the movable property of Gongfa Company's Chinese and Western pharmacies and hot spring bathhouses in the Special District Court today, and it has been approved. The Chinese and Western pharmacy has already received a bid of 240,000 yuan, and the hot spring bathhouse has received a bid of 50,000 yuan. If there is a change on the part of the receiver after the seizure, the loss of the future prospects will be unimaginable. For the benefit of the creditors, we request that a way be found to stop it as soon as possible to avoid losses. The lawyer Jiang Yiping stated that although our lawyer is handling the case jointly with Wu Jingxiong and others, the request to the Special District Court was handled entirely by Lawyer Wu alone. It is best to ask the court to send an accountant and a bailiff to Lawyer Wu's office to find a way to stop it. Judge Gong Chengshen said that with the prestige of this court, it is impossible to send someone to beg Lawyer Wu to find a way, etc. As a result, Lawyer Jiang assumed the responsibility of accompanying Accountant Pan to Wu Jingxiong's office to find a way to stop the seizure. After they left, the court continued the hearing. The two directors, Zhou Songqing and Chen Xingwu, also defended themselves through lawyers, stating that their clients were not directors and that there was no definite evidence for the plaintiff's accusations. They also requested dismissal. The plaintiff's lawyer, Yan Luqing, stated that director Zhou Songqing was not only a director but also a relative of Huang Chujiu's family. How can he deny it? He requested a clear investigation. The judge ordered to wait for a decision. The lawyer representing Yuan Ludeng stated that although his client was a director, all decisions were made by Huang Chujiu alone, and he never obtained considerable benefits. Now that Huang's private property can be used as collateral, there is no need to seek compensation from the directors. The plaintiff's lawyer, Chen Zhigao, stated that since Yuan Ludeng has admitted to being a director, he requested that the case be summoned and questioned about the responsibility of other shareholders. This case can be easily resolved immediately. The lawyer Tan Yigong, representing Huang's family, stated that this case had previously been ordered by the court to hand over Huang's property for sale. Subsequently, our lawyer received the court order forwarded by the Special District Court and immediately transferred the property to the accountant. Unexpectedly, our lawyer recently received several letters from creditors, pointing out that our lawyer had not handed over Huang's property, etc. Our lawyer was very surprised. The creditors have different claims, either suing in this court or requesting provisional attachment of movable property from the Special District Court. May I ask whether this kind of behavior is legitimate? The plaintiff's lawyer, Xu Yannian, also stated that our lawyer also believes that the seizure of movable property by the Special District Court is inappropriate. I don't know what the intentions of the other creditors are. It should be investigated. Judge Gong Chengshen ordered the hearing to be adjourned for fourteen days.

U.S. General Motors Company Expands Business

U.S. General Motors Company, established for two years, has offices in Shanghai and Shenyang, China, but they are affiliated with the Osaka, Japan headquarters. Now, for the purpose of expanding its business, the company will reorganize the Shanghai office as an independent organization, appointing Mr. Anger as president and general manager. Mr. Miles, together with his wife and two sons, arrived in Shanghai from Kobe, Japan, a few days ago to take office and will be stationed in Shanghai permanently. Mr. Kerkis, the former acting manager of the Shanghai branch, has already requested leave to return to New York. Hereafter, Mr. Guo will be fully responsible for the business of General Motors in China and Manchuria. The company's staff has also been replaced with new people, but the company's agents remain unchanged. Mr. Miles has been the assistant manager of the headquarters since 1929 and a member of the supervisory committee of the Japanese company. He is very familiar with the situation of General Motors. In 1915, Mr. Miles worked for the Gallant Car Company. From 1920 to 1923, he was the general representative of General Motors in China, Japan, and the Philippine Islands. His headquarters were initially located in Manila and later moved to Shanghai. In 1923, he opened branches in Melbourne, Australia, and resided there for three years. Later, due to personal affairs in Arizona, he resigned from his position. Mr. Miles is very enthusiastic about public affairs and club activities. He has been an active member of the Rotary Club for many years and was formerly the president of the American Club in Melbourne. Recently, he was the president of the Washington Society in Kobe and a member of the Kobe Club. Mr. Miles has such a long history and rich experience in the automobile business, and now that he has been appointed as the president of the China headquarters, his contributions to China will be considerable, and his business in China will surely develop greatly and prosper, which can be predicted.

A photo of Mr. Miles is attached.

Large-Scale Suppression of Bandits by Land, Sea, and Air

▲In Order to Protect Fishermen

Sea bandits outside Wusongkou are rampant. During the fishing season, coastal fishermen do not dare to go to sea and have petitioned the authorities to send warships to protect them. It is learned that the Jiangsu Provincial Government's Pacification Superintendent's Office, the National Coastal Defense Office, and the Wusong Water Police Fourth District have jointly established the Jiangsu Coastal Fishing Protection Temporary Office in Nantong. The province has allocated 20,000 yuan in funding and appointed Zhang Han, the chief of the Water Police Fourth District, as the commander-in-chief of bandit suppression, and Ding Moxiang, the section chief of the Coastal Defense Office, as an advisor. On the sea, naval warships Tongji, Shui Jing Ce Dian, Pingyang, Zhenhai, Jinghai, and other gunboats, as well as patrol boats of the Seventeenth and Eighteenth Squadrons, have been mobilized, advancing on land and sea to encircle and suppress the bandit lair in Da'an Port. The headquarters has also dispatched seaplanes to assist, it is said.

Chen Mutao

The Truth of Embezzlement

▲Helping His Younger Brother Misappropriate Public Funds

▲Feared Understanding and Attempted Suicide by Taking Medicine

Chen Mutao from Jiahe, the deputy director of the savings department of the Zhejiang Industrial Bank, suddenly claimed to be ill and entered the Shanghai Public Hospital a few days ago. At the same time, the bank discovered that he had embezzled 64,000 yuan in savings deposits and filed a complaint with the police, who moved Chen to the Municipal Council Hospital for treatment, pending a trial after he recovered. This has been briefly reported in this newspaper. The matter seemed rather strange at first, and the details were unclear. However, after the court opened the trial yesterday, the truth gradually emerged. Chen Mutao had served in the Zhejiang Industrial Bank for 14 years and had always maintained his integrity, which was valued by the bank manager. He was initially given the position of deputy director of the savings department. Chen was not only very sincere in dealing with people but also had a deep love for his younger brother. Because his younger brother had certain needs, he could not bear to stand by and watch. He then secretly misappropriated bank funds to help him, allowing his brother to be relieved of economic pressure. Chen was generous and would always help friends who asked for assistance, using funds misappropriated from the bank. This kind of behavior was equivalent to spending other people's money generously. Over time, he incurred a deficit of more than 64,000 yuan. His brother was unable to make amends, and he feared that once the matter was revealed, even with a hundred mouths, it would be difficult to obtain understanding. He would be ruined and discredited, and how could he avoid it? Ten days ago, he decided to commit suicide. On the first day of this month, he wrote a letter to the bank manager, detailing the process and purpose of misappropriating the funds. He stated at the end that he felt ashamed of his duties but regretted that it was too late. What face did he have to live in the world? He could only repay with his death. He begged the bank to consider the many years of working together and to refrain from pursuing the matter after his death. On the same day, he went to Wusong alone, telling people that he was going to the countryside for a stroll. He secretly bought two bottles of sleeping pills and took them with him. Arriving at Songjiang, he briefly toured the beach, planning to drown himself in the sea at night. He went to a beachside hotel for a temporary rest. When midnight came and all was quiet, he quietly left the hotel, thinking he could follow Qu Yuan. Unexpectedly, there were iron gates outside the hotel door, making it difficult to cross the line. Sighing at the ocean, his desire to die grew stronger. He returned to his room, drank all the poison, and went to the fence, wanting to get over it. However, as soon as he jumped up, he fell backward and fainted on the ground. He was then spotted by someone. By this time, the power of the medicine had reached his internal organs, and he had lost consciousness. People then sent him back to Shanghai and into the Shanghai Public Hospital. The previous report that he went to the hospital due to illness was a false rumor. The next day, the general police station sent detectives to the Municipal Council Hospital for treatment after the bank filed a complaint accusing him of embezzlement, in order to facilitate the investigation. Fortunately, the rescue was successful, and all the poison he had taken was removed. Yesterday morning, the police sent Chen to the Special District Local Court, where Judge Xu Jiaxue interrogated him. Police lawyer Ru Baoyi explained the circumstances of the case and presented Chen's letter to the Zhejiang Industrial Bank for inspection. Chen also admitted to misappropriating 60,000 yuan and 2,900 taels of silver and requested leniency. Judge Xu then ordered the defendant to be remanded in custody, pending further investigation.

Xu Asan Falls from a Cart and Dies

A cargo truck from a certain company was driving near the Xiangyun Road racecourse in Jiangwan at around 4:00 PM the day before yesterday. The truck was loaded with four or five coolies. There were few pedestrians and vehicles on Xiangyun Road, and the truck driver sped up and drove straight ahead at full speed. A felt hat belonging to Xu Asan, a Jiangbei man among the coolies on the truck, was suddenly blown off by the wind. Asan immediately asked the truck driver to stop, but it was not easy to brake immediately at full speed. Asan, being impatient, jumped off before the truck stopped, falling heavily, causing his head to be smashed and his brains to spill out. He died instantly. The truck driver stopped the truck, sounded the alarm, and reported it to the Local Court for an examination. Yesterday afternoon, the prosecutor and others arrived to conduct the examination and ordered the truck owner to prepare a coffin and collect the body pending further investigation.

Chu Shaoting

Turned Back to Look at the Bandit's Face

▲Causing His Death

Chu Shaoting, a Henan native, is 31 years old. He previously served as a platoon leader under Zhao Jie, the commander of the Henan Garrison. Zhao was assassinated while in office a few years ago, and the troops were disbanded. Chu then returned to his hometown. He came to Shanghai last winter, wanting to seek a job with a friend of his former master Zhao. After arriving in Shanghai, it was difficult to find a suitable position for a while, and he temporarily stayed at the old master's residence in Hehefang, Xiafei Road, French Concession. He spent all the money he had brought and relied on loans from his fellow villagers or former colleagues to support his life as a traveler. Unexpectedly, at around 1:00 AM on February 20, Chu was walking alone in front of No. 248, Kaizi'er Road, west of the Great World in the French Concession, when he was suddenly encountered by a highway robber who blocked his path, showed a pistol, and threatened to rob him. They took off his leather robe. At the time, Chu did not dare to resist and allowed the bandits to do as they pleased. When the bandits were escaping with the stolen goods, Chu turned back to look at the bandits' faces and figures. The bandit immediately fired a shot at Chu with his pistol. The ruthless bullet hit Chu in the abdomen, and he fell to the ground. The bandit then fled. Later, patrolling police officers passed by and saw him and took him to the police station. Because he was injured, they could not ask his name at the time. The police chief ordered him to be sent to Renji Hospital for treatment before learning his name. However, due to his serious injuries, the treatment was ineffective, and he died at 6:00 PM on the 11th of this month. The hospital notified the police station, who carried the body to the Tongren Fuyuan Branch to examine it. It was determined that the deceased had died from a gunshot wound sustained during a robbery. They ordered photographs to be taken and allowed the friend of the deceased, Fei Liansheng, to prepare a coffin and collect the body, pending the police's arrest of the murderer for investigation.

The Corpse's Face Did Not Change Color

▲The Tragic Change in the Hou Family

▲Drank Tea Until Dawn and Died

Hou Chungen, a local resident of No. 12, Houjiazhai, Haige Road, West Shanghai, was 50 years old. He used to work as a handyman. He had a son named Jinfa, who is now 25 years old and not yet married. Jinfa lost his mother at the age of three and was raised by his maternal grandmother. In 1927, he went to a factory in Fengtian as a worker. He returned home last autumn and is now making a living by working in a foreign-owned flower garden near the Hongqiao Road airfield. His younger brother, Chunyu, is 42 years old and very fierce. He is currently a carpenter in a Dongyang factory. His wife, Ren, is even more shrewish. They have two sons, the eldest, Quansheng, is 20 years old and drives a car, and the younger, Quandi, is 17 years old and works as a shop assistant in a foreign firm. The two brothers live in the same house but cook separately. However, Chungen and his son were weak and often subjected to abuse by Chunyu and his wife, even treated like cattle and horses. Unexpectedly, on the evening of the 6th of this month, Chungen suddenly died of a sudden illness. The next day, family members notified the deceased's son, Jinfa, to return home to handle the funeral. Jinfa saw that his father's death was strange and was suspicious, but he dared to be angry but did not dare to speak out. Moreover, his family was very poor, and he had no funds for any expenses. He thought that his deceased father had five fen of land in his name, worth about 2,000 yuan. The land deed had long been mortgaged by Chunyu. He then asked for it back so that he could borrow money for the funeral. Unexpectedly, Chunyu and his wife refused to hand it over and were unreasonable. Jinfa had no choice but to report it to the local police station. Police Chief Zhang Xiangrui went to mediate but was beaten. Ren also threw dirty things from the chamber pot at them. The police then took Chunyu and his wife, along with the deceased's son Hou Jinfa, back to the Second Division of the Sixth District. After a brief interrogation by Chief Liu, Hou Jinfa stated the previous situation. Hou Chunyu confessed that the deceased's wife had sent tea to the room on the evening of the 6th and did not know he was dead until dawn. However, the deceased's brother had 2.5 fen of land left in his name, and he was willing to pay for the funeral, but Jinfa did not agree. Chief Liu believed that the case involved a property dispute and was an insult to public officials. He transferred the case to the court on the 9th of this month for trial. The night before, Patrol Chief Zhang led the police on patrol to Houjiazhai. According to reports from the villagers, the body had not yet been buried and had recently been found to have injuries. Chief Zhang believed that the case was serious and reported it to the chief. Chief Liu went to inspect it himself out of prudence. He saw that the corpse's face had not changed color and that there were indeed bluish-purple marks on his chest. Fearing that it would rot and be unsanitary, he ordered the local guarantor Wang Zipei to report it for an examination. Yesterday afternoon, at around 1:00 PM, the court appointed Prosecutor Yang Qi to bring a coroner to the scene for an examination. The examination revealed that the deceased had died from poison taken before death. He ordered the deceased's son to prepare a coffin for burial, pending instructions. Because he had no money to buy a coffin, the Hou family raised money to pay for the burial, it is said.

French Concession Municipal Council

A Car Crashes and Kills Jiang Hongmei

▲Lawyers Argue with Each Other

▲The Judge Ordered a Recess to Wait for the Verdict

Li Xianming, a driver for the French Concession Municipal Council, was driving truck number 755 at the intersection of Lafayette Road and Pingjili Road, No. 119, at 3:00 PM on the 25th of last month when he crashed into and killed Hongmei, the six-year-old daughter of Jiang Wenhua from Chengli, De Renli, No. 9. Yesterday, the police sent Li to the French Court for questioning. First, the police chief from the car department reported the circumstances of the accident at the time. Then, the witness Shen Yongjian stated that he was passing by the area that day and saw the child being run over and killed by the defendant's truck's rear wheel. The defendant, Li Xianming, stated that he was driving on Lafayette Road that day and saw the child standing by the side of the road. Therefore, he continued to drive forward, not knowing how the child suddenly was run over by the rear wheel. The plaintiff, Jiang Wenhua, represented by lawyer Di Baike, stated that according to the defendant's confession, he saw the child standing on the side of the road. At that time, the defendant should have stopped at any time and waited for the child to cross the road before continuing to drive. The defendant ignored it and continued to drive forward, causing the disaster. He is undoubtedly to blame. In addition to this child, there is also a one-year-old boy in the plaintiff's family. The plaintiff's wife became ill with anxiety after her eldest daughter was killed. The two-year-old child also died from drinking the sick mother's milk. The situation is very miserable. The disaster was caused by the defendant alone. He requested that the defendant be prosecuted according to the law and requested 10,000 yuan in private compensation. The defendant, represented by lawyer Bahe, argued that the defendant, of course, apologized for the death of the plaintiff's child. However, in fact, the defendant was not at fault. The defendant's driver was driving very slowly that day. Although he saw the child standing by the side of the road, he did not know that the child suddenly walked out, causing him to be run over by the rear wheel. The defendant has been in office for many years and has never had any faults. The plaintiff's child was only six years old. How could he be allowed to walk in the middle of the road? The parents should bear considerable responsibility. Shanghai is densely populated, and there are many vehicles on the road. If the car driver had to stop every time he saw a person, traffic in Shanghai would be immediately cut off. This case should not only not be compensated for losses, but also be rejected. The Chinese and Western officials ordered a recess to wait for the verdict.

Fire in a Printing Shop Burns Several People

▲Two Apprentices Break Their Arms and Legs

Shuntai Printing Bureau, located at Nos. 789-790, Shunqingli, Qipu Road, suddenly caught fire around 5:00 AM yesterday. Instantly, thick smoke filled the air, and flames spread everywhere. The shop owner, Gong Rulin, his wife, children, workers, and others were awakened from their dreams and fled for their lives. However, the paper and ink piled in the shop were extremely flammable. In a blink of an eye, the stairs were burned off. Then, they jumped down from the windows of the building, with more than ten people injured and burned. The Hongkou Fire Brigade received the news and immediately drove to the scene to extinguish the fire. After about a quarter of an hour, the fire was slightly reduced. By the time it was completely extinguished, it was already dawn. When the fire was raging, the apprentices Ma Changgen, Yuan Yongchang, and Zhang Kunsong all jumped down from the third-floor loft window to escape, breaking their arms and legs and suffering serious injuries. The shop owner, Gong Rulin, his wife, Wu, and their children, Amao and Aying, were also injured and were sent to Tongren and Guangren Hospitals by the fire brigade for treatment. The cause of the fire is unknown, but it is known that it started from the loft. The names of the injured are as follows: Ma Changgen, 14 years old, from Zhaopu, injured his head; Yuan Yongchang, 19 years old, from Pinghu, broke his left leg; Zhang Kunsong, 15 years old, local, broke his right hand; Gong Rulin, 42 years old, from Wuxi, injured his head and hands; his wife, Wu, and children Aying, Amao, and Heshang, suffered minor injuries; wet nurse Ding Lu, maid Zhou Chen, and typesetter Xu Haiguan suffered various head and back injuries.

▲Continued Interrogation of the Defendants' Statements

▲Waiting for the Next Continued Trial and Debate

The case of Xu Yan, the captain of the water patrol team, for embezzlement, was reopened yesterday afternoon by Judge Shen. The court (asked) Xu Yan, was the first opium found on September 14? (Answered) I have recorded it clearly. (Asked) Now, the Public Security Bureau has replied that you requested leave on September 16 for only six days. (Answered) There is a case for it. I was ill. (Asked) The second batch of red pills does not need to be investigated. (Answered) This is completely not the case. (Asked) Did you swallow the raw opium with the intention of selling it? (Answered) I did not take it. (Asked) Why did you release the soldiers and traffickers Xing Genda and Shen Liansheng in the third opium case? (Answered) Since I released the people, how could I leave the opium in the team? (Asked) If it was not your order, how could you release them? (Answered) If it was my order, it should have a seal. (Asked) Is Zhang Longfa the same as Zhang Yuting? (Answered) Yes, it is. Xing Genda and Shen Liansheng hired me to load raw opium onto the Daji ship. I did not know about it. (Asked) Did you discuss the price? (Answered) No. (Asked) How many times have you done this kind of good business? (Answered) Once. (Asked) How did you not discuss the price once? (Answered) Rowing a boat is like a rickshaw. BL Society's Intimidation Letter

▲Gu Xingsheng Remains Calm

▲Lin Amao Is Extremely Bored

Gu Xingsheng, a Suzhou native, 45 years old, lives at No. 102, Xiaopi Lane, and runs Gu Renji Silk and Satin Glue Workshop, specializing in dyeing plain fabrics for various shops. Because there are few such businesses in Shanghai, the profits are still high. However, Gu likes to raise birds and live a secluded life, leaving the workshop to his son to manage. In recent years, it has been smooth. Unexpectedly, he was targeted by bandits. On March 28, he received a threatening letter from the post office, extorting 2,000 yuan. It was agreed that at 10:00 PM on the 29th, the money should be delivered to the Xianshi World Beijing Opera Theater, and the person carrying the money must hold a white foreign bottle as a sign, and someone would come to contact him. The signature was "BL Society President Qi", with a rubber stamp. After receiving the letter, Gu Xingsheng smiled and dismissed it. On the 31st, he received another letter, again agreeing to deliver the money to the letterbox hanging on the No. 110 pole at the entrance of Chengzhili Second Lane, Yangjiazhai, Xinkaihe at 12:00 PM on April 1. It was explained that the package should be wrapped in red paper and a red paper strip should be pasted on the pole as a sign. Because Gu had no enemies in peacetime and lacked funds, he did not pay attention to it. Who knew that on April 7, he received another letter, saying that on the day of the previous agreement, he did not see him because of the rain. He agreed to pay the money at the same address at 12:00 PM on April 12. On the 9th, another letter came, with strong words, saying that if he did not fulfill the agreement, he would take appropriate measures. Later, the Public Security Bureau of the Second Division of the First District learned of the previous situation. Gu presented the letter and asked for arrest. Unexpectedly, on the 8th, another letter came, changing the agreement to deliver the money to the letterbox hanging on the No. 15 pole at the intersection of Yanhai Road and Zihua Road in Guangfu Temple at 12:00 PM that night. The Second Division of the First District, in conjunction with the First Division of the Second District, led police officers and waited several nights but found no trace. After strict investigation and reports, it was learned that the principal offender, Lin Amao, was hiding in the house at No. 5, Wangshengfang, Anrenli, Anren Street. At 3:00 AM yesterday, Section Chief Yi led Magistrate Ma and police officers to search and arrest him. The suspect heard the sound and tried to escape, but he was caught by police officer Man Zhaogan and taken to the station for interrogation. According to the confession, Lin Amao is 26 years old, a Ningbo native, with one sister and one younger sister. He used to be a machinist, but he lost his job due to a fracture in his left hand. He had no way to make a living, so he had this unrealistic idea. The threatening letter was indeed written by him. He used to be a classmate with Gu Xingsheng's son, so he knew the economic situation of his family in detail, but he had no accomplices. When he was arrested, a fake pistol and three rubber stamps with various forms of the BL Society were found. Section Chief Yi believed that the case was not that simple and sent it to the General Public Security Bureau for interrogation today.

Barber's Suicide

▲ Overwhelmed by Gambling Losses

▲ Ashamed of Brother's Theft

Bian Jinshun, a Yangzhou native only twenty-three years old, worked as a barber at Caitong Barber Shop, No. 434 Jiangxi Road. His younger brother, Jinli, was an apprentice carpenter at Xie Yongxing Woodworking in Zhabei. Jinshun was addicted to gambling, and all his earnings throughout the year were squandered at the gambling table. In recent days, his gambling urge intensified, but his luck worsened, resulting in substantial losses. Just as resentment was mounting and he felt helpless, he suddenly

Page 12

heard the news that his brother had been severely reprimanded for stealing the master's property at the woodworking shop, leaving him even more ashamed. Last Saturday night, Jinshun was restless and unable to sleep due to his troubled mind. When he heard the morning rooster crow, he suddenly felt utterly hopeless and devoid of interest in life. He found a damaged electric wire in the room, hanged himself. By the time dawn broke, Wang Xiaosizi, his roommate, woke up from his dream and saw Jinshun's feet dangling in the air. He quickly untied him, but he was already ice-cold, his tongue protruding, and he had breathed his last. The shop owner, Zhou Yongcai, reported to the General Inspector's Office, which sent detectives to carry the body to the Forensic Examination Office on Fielun Road. Yesterday, Prosecutor Qian from the Special District Court, after inspecting the body, ordered the deceased's elder brother, Bian Jinan, to claim the body for burial.

Li Xiuying Accuses Husband of Abandonment

▲ Defendant Claims Non-Formal Union

▲ Judge Encourages Reconciliation Outside Court

Li Zhixin, a native of Yuyao, previously married Li Xiuying, a young woman from Ningbo, and is now accused of abandonment. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Ge of the Special District Local Court conducted a hearing. According to Li Xiuying's complaint, she married the defendant on the eighth day of the fourth month of the seventeenth year (of the Republic), and they had a very harmonious relationship. They have a son, Zhonghua, who is now three years old, and she is currently pregnant and will soon give birth. However, since the last quarter of last year, the defendant suddenly changed his behavior and abandoned her. The defendant works at Kodak Company, earning a monthly salary of over one hundred yuan. Mr. Wu, a colleague of his, mediated when they first fell out and arranged for the defendant to provide forty-five yuan per month for household expenses, but this stopped abruptly in January of this year. Recently, while she was visiting her mother's home for the holidays, he secretly moved all the household items away, treating her like a stranger, forcing her to file a lawsuit. In response, Li Zhixin claimed that his relationship with the plaintiff was a non-formal union, without the establishment of a marital relationship. He also stated that he was currently unable to make ends meet and asked the plaintiff to return to her hometown to live with his mother, and that he had not abandoned her. Judge Ge ruled that the case could not be self-prosecuted under the law and dismissed it. He also encouraged both parties to reconcile outside of court, giving them ten days to do so. If a reconciliation is not reached within the time limit, the woman should report to the police station, and the case will be reviewed after a public prosecution.

Labor Dispute on Gonghe Wheel Heard Yesterday

Since the comprador Shen Huating of the British firm Jardine Matheson's Gonghe Wheel had an armed clash with eighty veteran workers in Wuhu last month, Shen resigned and has now been succeeded by Chen Bonian. The eighty veteran workers are members of the Seamen's Union. In addition, there are thirty-eight workers who are not members of the union but have been working on the ship for more than three years. Comprador Chen wanted to dismiss all thirty-eight of them immediately upon taking office, so the workers rose up in opposition. After repeated unsuccessful mediation by the Social Bureaus of Shanghai and Hankou, the matter was submitted to the Hankou Municipal Government for arbitration. The Ministry of Industry and Commerce also sent a supporting telegram, designating the Hankou Municipal Government as the competent administrative authority for the case, ordering it to promptly arbitrate and setting the 15th of this month as the arbitration date. Before a resolution is reached, the workers were ordered to continue working on the ship as usual and not to take rash action. Unexpectedly, when the ship returned to Shanghai from Hankou the day before yesterday (the 7th), Comprador Chen, after the ship left port, completely removed the nameplates from the thirty-eight workers' berths, immediately suspending their work. Unable to resist, the workers came to Shanghai in distress and immediately petitioned the Shanghai Municipal Party Headquarters and the Social Bureau to uphold justice. A discussion was held at the Social Bureau that day, and representatives from the Municipal Party Headquarters also attended. Comprador Chen did not attend, only representatives from both sides of the workers attended, arguing for a long time without any result. They are waiting for the arbitration of the Hankou Municipal Government. The ship is scheduled to arrive in Hankou this afternoon, and arbitration will take place tomorrow.

Seamen Should Receive Pay Raise as Agreed

The Chinese Seamen's Industrial Joint Federation issued a notice yesterday to the stokers, deckhands, and stewards of all Shanghai steamships, stating that according to a report from Liu Yuzhou, secretary of the federation, the federation signed an agreement with the Shanghai Shipping Association last year to increase the salaries and food allowances of stokers, deckhands, and stewards on all Shanghai steamships, with the third article stipulating that starting March 1st, 1921, the monthly salaries and food allowances of these seamen would be increased by an additional ten percent, equivalent to two large silver dollars in general currency. The period has now arrived, and the association should be instructed to fulfill the agreement, and the seamen should be notified to comply with the previous agreement and fully honor the contract. Therefore, the federation is reporting to the board and requesting verification and implementation. In addition to instructing the association to fulfill the agreement, a notice is hereby issued that all seamen of the respective departments should, starting March 1st of this year, request an additional two dollars in salary per month from the relevant shipping companies and must not allow for any delay or arrears. Special announcement. Chairman Zhao Zhizhi, Committee Members Lin Yinsheng, Liang Degong, Huang Yushu, Zhao Shuizhang, April 10th.

Relief Committee

Distributes Spring Relief Funds to Various Provinces

The National Government Relief Committee previously received one million yuan in cigarette bonds approved by Chairman Chiang for distribution to various provinces for disaster relief. The committee had previously pawned the bonds to the Shanghai, China, Communications, Zhongnan, Zhejiang Industrial, and Four Banks Savings Association for a total of 500,000 yuan and, at a meeting last year, decided to distribute the funds to various provinces for winter relief. Now, because spring relief is urgent, the bonds have been sold at market price. After deducting the principal and interest owed to the banks, there is still 300,000 yuan remaining. The committee, at its 14th committee meeting, allocated funds based on the severity of the disaster situation in each province. The allocated amounts are listed below: 47,000 yuan to Henan, 47,000 yuan to Gansu, 30,000 yuan to Jiangxi, 25,000 yuan to Hunan, 10,000 yuan to Fujian, 20,000 yuan to Anhui, 20,000 yuan to Jiangsu, 3,000 yuan to Chahar, 3,000 yuan to Suiyuan, 5,000 yuan to Heilongjiang, 6,000 yuan to Sichuan, 10,000 yuan to Guizhou, 5,000 yuan to Ningxia, 5,000 yuan to Shandong, 10,000 yuan for relief in Hao County, Anhui, 20,000 yuan for relief and canal construction in Longdong, Shaanxi, and 7,000 yuan for soup kitchens. The Director of the Shanghai Office of the Committee, Mr. Gong Yiting, has already transferred the funds to the respective provinces to rush the spring relief efforts.

Cattle Plague Outbreak in Wangjiang, Anhui

▲ Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau Sends Personnel for Relief

Wangjiang, Anhui, is an important agricultural area in Anhui Province. Recently, a severe cattle plague has broken out. It is reported that over a thousand heads have died in the past month. Because the area is remote, there is nowhere to buy serum. Farmers are generally letting nature take its course and cannot save the animals. After receiving the news, the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau, noting that it produces a large quantity of cattle plague serum and that its efficacy is very great, sent personnel to inject the serum when cattle plague broke out in Shanghai and Zhenjiang, Jiangsu last year. The results were excellent, and countless cattle were saved. The bureau's cattle plague serum is usually priced very low, and free injections can also be provided when necessary. The cattle plague in Wangjiang is raging and has a great impact on farmers. The bureau has sent technician Shou Biao to provide free injections to provide relief. It is reported that Shou Biao set off today.

Letter to the Editor

Dear Editor:

I am writing in response to a news item in your newspaper's news column on the 12th of this month entitled "Recent News on the Day and Night Bank Creditors' Group (Requests Evidence of Bian Jialu's Repayment)," which is not in accordance with the facts. I am writing to request a correction as follows: My firm's employee, Xu Bingru (also known as Xu Jian), was suspended from his position on the 1st of this month for improper conduct. He left without waiting for the transfer to be completed, falsely claiming that he introduced 2,000 creditors for the Day and Night Bank and the Great World Savings Department's creditor registration, which was handled by this law office. It should be noted that this lawyer was first entrusted by the initiators of the creditors to handle the registration, and other creditors joined successively, all coming directly of their own volition. Xu served in the firm and could not have been the one who introduced them. He has no responsibility in this regard. Xu was hired on a monthly salary basis and had no right to share in the public fees. I am writing to request that your newspaper investigate and make a correction.

Sincerely,

Lawyer Bian Jialu, April 13, 20th year of the Republic
