Xie Wuliang and Wuji

— Qing Lin

Under revolutionary politics. There is a Control Yuan. Its organization. I won't elaborate. Examining its nature. It is the censorate of the Qing Dynasty. And the Office of the Censor during Yuan Shikai's time. Established specifically to clarify politics. And impeach high officials. The supervisors. Have been sworn into office. For many days. Among them, it seems that most are from Shaanxi. And Xie Wuliang is one of them. Xie is from Sichuan. Also a great writer in Sichuan. Many people today mistake Xie for a monk. This is a great mistake. Because the Xie family is not without monks. But he is an uncle. Not a brother. Xie's brothers are ten in all. All are outstanding. Wuliang is second. The third is Wuji. Dharma name Wanhui. He is a true monk. That is, the one that the world mistakenly identifies as Wuliang. Wanhui once studied Buddhism in India. His writing. Definitely has a little Bodhi nectar. Sprinkle the wonders of six thousand. Sometimes it is like a light cloud in the sky. Flying around the silent cold moon. Sometimes it is like a celestial horse galloping through the sky. Carrying mountains and surpassing seas. The so-called study of spirituality. Combining rigidity and softness. If he utters his lion's roar. He will immediately awaken the stubborn and deaf. Immediately put down the butcher knife. However, Wuliang himself. Is not ordinary either. At the age of twelve or thirteen. He lectured in Sichuan. Hundreds of people followed. Then his intelligence and courage. Can be imagined. If one only praises him as a prodigy. One is truly not a confidant of Wuliang. It is said that Wuliang is not good at Western learning. But by translating and looking up dictionaries. He can actually go on stage to give lectures on Western history. Is this not a heaven-sent writing talent? When he was stranded at sea. He rented a small hut in front of the county office. Earning a living as a beggar by selling his writing. Barely supporting his wife and children. As for the beginning of his rise to fame. It was when Mr. Sun Zhesheng was ordered to persuade the Eastern Province. To persuade Zhang Zuolin to form a triangular alliance. At that time, Wuliang was specially appointed as Sun's secretary. Using chopsticks as a metaphor. Assisting between the altar and the temple. Calm and leisurely. With many brilliant ideas. Never disgracing the monarch's order. His contribution was great. Therefore, although he has floated and sunk many times. He is now finally known in his time as the important position of Supervisor. Alas. Human power is superior to heaven. Learning is heaven-sent. Heroic times. One cannot do without. The world mistakes Wuji for Wuliang. It is nothing more than saying that the Xie family produced two monks. Although it is said that one son becomes a Buddha. Nine generations ascend to heaven. The more, the better. There is no malice intended. However, Wuji alone cannot be submerged. According to what I know. I will specially clarify this.

The Jumping Over the Wall and Cooking Proposals

— Tao Zaidong

In Utopia. There is an organization. Spanning across the various cities. Direct level to the capital. The members of the group. Are all patriotic youth. Surveying the world at a glance. Politics are omnipotent. But writing is not their forte. My younger brother, Tao Zaixi. Once knew how to draft edicts with Lu Jingyu and Linghuzi. With a thin reputation for writing. So although he is old. He was still hired as a secretary. His monthly salary reached as much as hundreds of yuan. The livelihood of his family depended on it. One day, the group members reported on a wind disaster. Saying that there was a well in the group headquarters. Blown outside the wall by the wind. It was resolved to hand it over to the secretary to draft the document. My brother struggled to think. Fortunately, he was able to rationalize it. The general idea was that the group headquarters originally built the wall with wooden boards and bamboo fences. The corner of the wall was the well. On that day, the wind was too strong. Moving this fence inward. Passing over the wellhead. So for a time, it was rumored that the well was blown out of the wall. The group members all praised his wit. Another day, they reported on a diary. Saying that several members of the group. Were having lunch in the courtyard. Suddenly, in mid-air. There were several roast ducks hanging by the stove. Coming one after another. Eating them was very pleasant. It was resolved to hand it over to the secretary to draft the document. My brother also found a way to rationalize it. Saying that the neighbor was a restaurant. Just at the time when the cook was fighting in anger. Throwing the duck. Looking like it was flying. Another day, they reported on a flood. The resolution said. A boat loaded with stone mills capsized. Stone mills floated all over the water. This must be described in the presentation. My brother presented that the water rose to the trees. The boat capsized at that spot. The stone mill has a wooden handle. The handle has a vertical piece of wood like a hook for holding. The hook hangs on the branches. No different from floating water. At this time, Secretary Tao's name in official documents was greatly praised. However, the material was light and the task was heavy. Heaven could not be relied on repeatedly. Before long, my brother's end had come. One day, the group discussed a parade. The route passed through a narrow lane. The lane was blocked by a high wall of considerable height. Some suggested opening a hole in the wall to pass. Opponents said that it was close to exploitation. Not possible. Some suggested detouring. Opponents said that it violated the original intention. Also not possible. Some suggested demolishing the wall. Opponents said. This group has creation. No destruction. Moreover, there is no money for demolition. While they were discussing. The leader suggested. There are no difficult words in the dictionary. When the time comes, the entire group will set off. With a great spirit of fearlessness. Demolishing the spirit of non-compromise. Everyone will jump over. At this time, the entire scene was tense. Unanimously agreed to pass. Handed over to the secretary to draft a notice to join the parading agency. Three days later, he could not hand in the paper. The leader was furious. My brother said. Dead ducks fly into the hands of the living. The wellhead moves to the movable wall. As for the stone mill, a handle-less shutter sinks. I am ashamed that my statement only fulfills half of it. Now, the jumping over the wall proposal. The grammar is to this point. Playing is exhausted. The only thing left is to pack up and leave. Returning and meeting my other brother, Tao Zainan. Also returned after resigning from another similar organization. Startled and asked. Zainan said. My brother was denounced for jumping over the wall. I was destroyed by the cooking proposal. Because my group discussed this case. Investigation-style must be used. Also clearly stating the law of cause and effect. The so-called scientific method. I followed the steaming of rice. Cooking rice. Pot rice. Immortal rice. The types are like eight-treasure rice and egg fried rice. Northern wheat rice. The time of death, such as breakfast, lunch, and dinner, are investigated in detail. Sending the draft after three days was not okay. There was a result but no cause. Before the rice was rice. Rice is like Gao Xianjian, the cover of Gao Baixianjing, and other types. Fortunately, there is a rice market to inquire about. Listed as a table. Sending the draft again after three days was still not okay. There is still a cause for rice. So before the rice was grain. Before the grain was rice. Before the rice was seedlings. Before the seedlings, one seed-by-seed was listed in the same way. Still not okay. The source of the seed must be traced before it is thorough. Before the seed, it is rice and grain. The cycle of inquiry. Even the righteous Shennong Houzhong could not find the cause. This is why I broke my rice bowl. So we sighed in front of each other. Changing the industry to peddlers.

Remembering Zhang Baosan

— Zhan Zhan

Old friend Wang Yanshi from Kunshan. Wrote the eight volumes of the Suihantang Anthology. Among them, there is a story about Zhang Baosan. Quite strange and interesting. It is a pity that the text is too long. Cannot be fully recorded. Extract the main points. To fulfill this talk. To give to the reader.

An'ting Town in Jiading County. Mr. Gui Zhenchuan of the Ming Dynasty. Once studied in that place. During the Daoguang period of the Qing Dynasty. There was a man named Zhang Baosan in the town. A rogue. Acquainted with a clerk in the provincial office. Quite familiar with the government. Once there were two families, Hu and Fu, in the area. Arguing over a woman in a lawsuit. Hu's reason was wrong but he was rich. So he hired Zhang and bribed the officials with 20,000 taels of silver. The prison was released. Zhang divided the money and did some small good deeds in the countryside. The people in the town praised him. Later, someone repaired the Bodhi Temple. Obtained Mr. Zhenchuan's portrait from the forehead. Zhang then built three houses on the side. Supplying images in it. A place for scholars in the village to gather and write. And slightly give money to give awards. So the scholars in the town. Also praised it. One year. There was a drought in the county. But Minglun, the magistrate of Jiading, took a trip to the town to investigate the famine. Discussed relief with the gentry at the Literary Meeting place. Hearing about Zhang's character. Strange. Called to speak. Very happy. He entrusted the relief to him. So Zhang was able to be listed among the gentry. Later, Tao Wenyi Shu. Moved to Jiangsu. Met the emperor in Beijing. The emperor loved reading Mr. Zhenchuan's writings. Ordered Tao to visit him after taking office. After Tao took office. He only got Gui Tian in the butcher shop. Ordered to change his name. Pulled into the martial arts academy. Afterwards, I wanted to build a Mr. Zhenchuan Academy. Difficult to find the person. It happened that he was subordinate to the East and came to visit. Tao spoke about the reason. But he raised Zhang to reply. Tao called to speak. Also unhappy. He entrusted the matter of the academy to him. And ordered sixty-three states and counties. Split the cost of construction. By the time the academy was completed. All famous public officials. Poets and poets. Come from thousands of miles away. Xiao Guan ran through the clouds. Singing all night long. Was called a grand event for a while. And Zhang's name also became famous. Later, Zhang rebuilt the first house behind the hospital. Married into a famous family. Now a family. Later, Tao left office. Lin Wenzhong replaced him. Visited the Mr. Zhenchuan statue at the academy. Actually split the court with Zhang. The rest of the officers below are needless to say. In my opinion, Tao and Lin are both famous ministers. I heard that But is also a follower. Zhang was a rogue. He was able to win his favor. Name became famous. The family is rich. Is it not strange? Wang also said that Zhang didn't know how to read. Want to write a letter. Dictating to others to write it. All have their reasons. Traveling with dignitaries. Improvise in the flower-flying game. Ancient poems and idioms. Come out of the mouth. At the time of building the academy. Its picture also came out of Zhang's hands. Pavilions. Ponds and stones, flowers and trees. All have the right location. Then Zhang is also a strange person. It is appropriate that he was appreciated by the three men.

Flowers on the Beijing-Shanghai Railway Line

— Yan Yin

People always say that young women are a tool to comfort life. A gathering without beauties makes people unhappy, especially for travelers. In a lonely lamp and desolate house, one often feels a sense of desolate vastness. Brothels and entertainment venues arise to take advantage of this time, also to comfort the loneliness of travelers. On the arid roads of the Northwest, there are also so-called "highway prostitutes." Since the railway was built, this kind of livelihood has disappeared. Unexpectedly, even on the most prosperous Beijing-Shanghai train, there are those who ride the rails, rushing by, and engaging in the business of selling smiles. One morning, returning to Shanghai from the capital, I lingered on the platform, as the train had not yet left the depot. Suddenly, a charming woman appeared, about twenty-four or five years old, tall and graceful, wearing a light yellow long cheongsam, and sporting tortoiseshell-rimmed glasses. She was dressed in leather shoes and silk stockings, and carrying a handbag, resembling a female school teacher. She spoke with a Beijing accent. The ticket collectors and train attendants on the train all seemed to know her, nodding in greeting, and she responded with a smile. I felt that she was unlike ordinary female passengers catching the train, because her words and actions were frivolous and not dignified, easily discernible at a glance. I then asked a familiar train employee, "Who is she?" He smiled and said, "Don't you know? This is what they call a 'flower on the Beijing-Shanghai Railway Line.'" I heard that this woman claims to be the concubine of a certain warlord, traveling between Beijing and Zhenjiang several times a week, to attract lonely and sad travelers. With a few words and glances, she entices them, and they get off the train at Zhenjiang, using hotels as their platforms. Those coming from Zhenjiang use Xiaguan as their destination. If travelers recognize her, it's like driving a familiar car on a well-known road. However, this woman's footsteps are only found on the Nanjing-Zhenjiang section. It is said that there is another person operating from Changzhou to Wuxi and Suzhou. As for the Suzhou-Shanghai section, no one has yet taken over, because there are more beauties in this section, making it difficult to start. Alas, people's lives are declining, and it is difficult to make a living. The strong take risks, and the weak have no choice but to resort to this path. People speak of loving couples, but I compare myself to a lonely wild goose. How can one not feel even more emotional towards the "flowers on the Beijing-Shanghai Railway Line"?

Travelogue of India (23)

— Ling Hua

9th. I heard of someone familiar with the situation in Tibet and visited him. According to him, the current population of Tibet is about 3 million, divided into three sects: Black Sect, Red Sect, and Yellow Sect. All believe in Buddhism. The Black Sect is the original old school, with many Buddhist lay practitioners. The Red Sect was founded by Padmasambhava, who does not prohibit issues of men and women outside the monastery, but they are prohibited inside. Their lamas are called Gompas, and they hold a significant position in the belief of the general public. The Yellow Sect is a pure monastic sect, founded by Je Tsongkhapa. The current Dalai Lama is their Pope. There are three major monasteries in total. One is Zhebung, originally intended for 9,900 monks, but now has over 10,000. The second is Ganden, originally intended for 5,500 monks, but now has 6,000 to 7,000. The third is Sera, originally intended for 3,300 monks, but now has 4,000 to 5,000. All are growing daily. The influence of the Red Sect is mostly in the area of Yatung Pass on the border between Yunnan and Tibet. The Red Sect lamas also help the Yellow Sect because Tibetans believe in the law of the Chakravarti. Their lamas are like Popes. There is a strange thing, and it's hard to say if it's entirely superstition. After a lama dies, another lama is selected. They can predict in advance where they will be reincarnated and descend into the world. Then, they go to that place and bring back a three- or five-year-old child. They test him in public, taking the bowls and chopsticks used by the previous lama and mixing them among many other bowls and chopsticks, and having him choose. He can choose correctly without error. Then, after three times of using dough to divine, it is also permitted by the gods. He is then formally appointed as the next lama. The reasoning behind this is difficult to understand. Perhaps there is a secret technique involved, which is hard to say.

As for the Tibetan people's feelings towards China, they still cherish and remember it. The Dalai Lama also has not forgotten China, but is simply succumbing to pressure. Why? Today, England's management of Tibet has already reached a mature stage. On one hand, they control the southeast of Tibet from Burma and China through the Yunnan border, and on the other hand, they are building railways on three routes, all approaching Tibet. One railway from Buxa to Bhutan can be reached in just six days, reaching Lhasa, the capital city of Tibet where the Dalai Lama resides. Two routes to Lhasa take only seven days, and the third route from Kalimpong to Lhasa takes only sixteen or seventeen days. If anything happens, they can advance on four routes, taking a surrounding position with no escape. But if China sends troops to Tibet, it would still take two months to reach Tibet from Yunnan, and three months from Sichuan. The whip is beyond reach.

There are over 10,000 soldiers inside Tibet, with thousands of rifles. Some were left by China, some were sold by England, and some were sold by Russian merchants. There is also a factory that can manufacture them itself. There is a technician named Cai from Sichuan who studied in Japan and is now teaching Tibetans how to make cannons. Regarding the relationship between Tibet and China, after the Qianlong Emperor, the Manchu official Fu Kangan once led troops into Tibet to help Tibet defeat Nepal, because Nepal had started a war with Tibet. As a result, Nepal was defeated and paid tribute to China. Yue Zhongqi was a famous general who pacified Tibet. Recently, because of the demarcation of the Sichuan-Tibetan border, with the Kham region being assigned to Sichuan, the Tibetans were dissatisfied with Sichuan and sent troops into Tibet. The Tibetans attacked the Sichuan troops, and the Sichuan troops were defeated and retreated. Generally speaking, China mainly relies on the troops on the Sichuan border, making it not easy to pacify Tibet. Tibet has a standing army and can continue to mobilize tens of thousands of soldiers, it is said.

A certain country has long been plotting to take over Tibet, and now its power is already established. If China has any hope, it is only to connect with its people and reform its politics. Because today the Tibetan people's burdens are becoming heavier and heavier, with heavy taxes levied on cattle and horses. People harbor resentment. Temples are extremely rich, partly because people like to donate to temples after death, and partly because temples lend money. There is a lot of gold in Tibet, but the people don't know how to use it. Tibet produces little, only wool and musk. I see that their people are similar in race to Mongolians and Han Chinese, and not like Indians. Some Tibetans still keep queues.

Sales of Blue Woolen Cloth Plunge

Sales of woolen cloth have been good recently, with many merchants placing orders with foreign companies. However, sales of blue woolen cloth serge, which has been popular in recent years, have plunged. This is because its popularity has lasted for four years, and demand from domestic customers has suddenly decreased. People seem to favor the new and dislike the old. Currently, only blue flash Walter cloth and blue thin elephant skin raincoat cloth are still selling. Other blue fabrics, such as tweed, serge, Walter cloth, and flannel, are unlikely to see any activity.

Oil Market: White Tung Oil Spring Sales About to Start

Tung oil is normally a hot seller in the spring, but due to last year's sluggish business, sales have also decreased. White tung oil is mainly for export. Since the price of gold has risen, European and American foreign companies find it difficult to make a profit, and few are buying, which has dampened the market. A month ago, supply from Hankou was relatively strong, and the market was sluggish. Foreign companies dropped prices to 18.4 taels, but later rebounded to 20.067 taels as foreign companies slightly increased purchases. Now that inland sales are about to start, the local market is also gradually becoming more active. However, sources have long been ignoring Hankou tung oil, relying only on Hangzhou tung oil. Merchants have purchased two to three thousand loads from Hangzhou at a price of 31 yuan per load delivered to Shanghai, which is more economical than Hankou. It is said that Hangzhou merchants also have limited inventory. Oil presses in Jinhua, Lanxi, Fenshui, Tonglu, Yanzhou, and Quzhou sell immediately after pressing and do not accumulate inventory. Therefore, with high handling costs, the market will rise.

Metals: New Lead Wire Price Drops by 2.5 Qian

▲ Blue Lead Fixed Price Remarkably Soft

▲ New Lead Wire: The market for #16 to #25 has recently seen a surge in Eastern imports and a lack of sales, so standard prices have fallen by 2.5 "qian". #16 to #20 is selling for 13.5 taels, and #21 to #25 is selling for 19.5 taels. Yesterday's orders were mostly for small quantities. There were no large transactions. Overseas prices have reportedly plummeted by more than one pound, so local prices are unlikely to rebound.

▲ Blue Lead: Recently, overseas fixed prices have been remarkably soft, leading to a decrease in local prices. Foreign lead is estimated at 15.75 taels, and domestic lead at 15.4 taels, down by three to four "qian" from last week. It is said that general merchants are pessimistic due to the weakness in overseas markets, leading to a decline in local prices.

Book Review

The Yunnan Problem

— Tang Bin

Compiled by Hua Qiyun, published by Datong Bookstore

The fact that our countrymen are now gradually paying attention to the importance of border defense is a good sign for the revitalization of our nation. The Japanese attempts to control Manchuria and Mongolia, and the British eyeing of Tibet, are all worthy of our study. We must never allow our entire territory to be devoured by other countries. Even when a new issue arises in Manchuria and Mongolia, the Japanese are eager to be the first to notice. They will write about it extensively in their newspapers, giving it double the promotion, causing the people of the entire country to take special notice, stimulating their interest in research, and acting as a backing for the government's ambitions to seize Manchuria and Mongolia. At the same time, the government also sends specialists to Manchuria and Mongolia to investigate industries and survey resources every year, no less than several dozens to hundreds of people. As for collections of works on Manchuria and Mongolia, there are so many in Japan that they could fill a cow cart and make it sweat. From this, it can be seen how much attention they pay to our country's borders, and at the same time, it can be known the importance of the position it occupies. In our country, it is only now that some people are paying attention to this border issue, and collections of works on Manchuria, Mongolia, and Tibet are gradually appearing in bookstores. This, of course, is worth describing, so that our complete territory does not fall piecemeal into the hands of other countries, and so that our nation gradually becomes rich and strong. This is what the compatriots across the country hope for. Of course, the importance of the Manchuria, Mongolia, and Tibet issues is great, but the Yunnan issue cannot be ignored. Although it is the second-largest province in terms of area among the Eighteen Provinces, its situation and other important aspects are unmatched by any other province. Some people think that Yunnan is a remote border area and has nothing to do with the overall situation, but they do not know that Yunnan is located upstream of the other provinces and has the form of overturning the world. This can indeed be proven by geography and history.

Entering Sichuan from Yunnan means taking control of the upper reaches of the Yangtze River. Passing through Guizhou to Huangping Yuanjiang to reach Hunan means being able to influence the north. Heading east to Guangxi, following the West River downwards, also means being able to take control of the Pearl River Basin. Liu Weitan said, "China is like a melon, and Yunnan is its stem. If the stem is rotten, the whole melon is rotten." This statement has full meaning, and it can also be proven by historical records. In the preface to the book, the author states, "In the Shu Han Dynasty, when Zhuge Wuhou led his troops on a northern expedition, he first conquered the southern barbarians to eliminate future troubles. In the middle of the Tang Dynasty, Yunnan was conquered by Nanzhao, and China suffered great turmoil. In the Song Dynasty, in order to avoid the mistakes of the Tang Dynasty, they first conquered Dali, and the Southern Song Dynasty was annexed. Recently, during the National Protection War in the fourth year of the Republic of China, Cai E was also able to rebuild the republic by relying on a corner of Yunnan. All of these are real historical examples and cannot be compared with empty echoes." These are indeed accurate words. The author then states, "Although the importance of Yunnan's situation depends entirely on Burma and Vietnam for protection, since Burma was lost to Britain and Vietnam was annexed by France, Yunnan has felt that its defenses have been completely removed and is surrounded by powerful neighbors. The border between Yunnan and Vietnam is mostly large mountains and rivers, which can still keep people out, but the interlocking border between Yunnan and Burma has no support. Fortunately, there is still the natural barrier of the Savage Mountain, which can separate China and foreign countries and serve as a natural Great Wall. However, even this place, the British are unwilling to let go and want to include it in their territory. The British invasion of Pianma in the late Qing Dynasty and the recent invasion of Jiangxinpo are both obvious examples of British aggression against the Savage Mountain. If the Savage Mountain is occupied by the British, not only will Yunnan be in danger, but the neighboring provinces of Sichuan and Tibet will also suffer. At this critical moment, if we do not widely publicize it, we will only repeat the mistakes of losing Vietnam and Burma in the past." These are golden words that deserve the attention of our countrymen. Objectively examining Yunnan from the perspective of historical and geographical evidence, there is indeed a need to pay attention to it at present. It is imperative that we recommend this book, "The Yunnan Problem," compiled by Hua Jun, to the reader.

The book is divided into two parts, the first part discussing British and French imperialism and Yunnan, with three chapters: 1. The Origins of British and French Covetousness of Yunnan, (A) Yunnan's Position in China, (B) The Motives of British and French Encroachment on Yunnan; 2. The Sino-British Yunnan-Burma Problem, (A) British Exploration in Yunnan, (B) The Loss of Burma, (C) The Yunnan-Burma Treaty, (D) The Yunnan-Burma Supplementary Treaty; 3. The Sino-French Yunnan-Vietnam Problem, (A) The Loss of Annam, (B) Regulations on Trade along the Vietnamese Border, (C) Commercial Treaties, (D) Border Treaties, (E) Supplementary Commercial Treaties, (F) Supplementary Border Treaties, (G) The Yunnan-Vietnam Railway Problem, (H) The Sino-French Convention. The second part discusses the Southwest Border Issue and Yunnan, with three chapters: 1. A General Overview of the Yunnan-Burma-Northwest Border Affairs, 2. The Pianma Problem, 3. The Jiangxinpo Problem. All of these are important in discussing the Yunnan problem. The author provides a concise description based on historical facts, which should also be understood by our general public.

Yunnan's position in China is undoubtedly very important. Although its area is the second largest among the Eighteen Provinces, its population is the second smallest among the Eighteen Provinces. Regarding this, the author has a detailed table in the book, comparing them one by one, so that we can understand that Yunnan is indeed a province with a vast land and a sparse population in China. This phenomenon is not due to Yunnan's poor land and poor people, but because it is located in a remote border area, and there are few immigrants. However, its products are rich in resources and surpass the other provinces, with copper and tin being the most important. The so-called natives have benefited greatly from this. Yunnan has both a vast land and abundant resources. However, on the one hand, it has a vast land and abundant resources, while on the other hand, it has a sparse population. In the situation of "vast land and abundant resources, but a sparse population," it is easy to be coveted by ambitious foreigners. There are already many examples of this on our borders, such as Japan's coveting of Southern Mongolia and Eastern Mongolia, and Russia's taking advantage of the situation in Northern Manchuria and Outer Mongolia. Therefore, the rise of Yunnan and the British and French covetousness of Yunnan are of course inevitable.

The attitude of British imperialists towards China has been clearly stated, and their covetousness of Yunnan, together with France, is not accidental. In the early years of the Tongzhi period of the Qing Dynasty, French merchants such as Ause and De Zhangbi secretly traveled to Yunnan along the rivers, exploring the terrain of the mountains and rivers and the rich mineral resources. Later, the French Du Pei entered Yunnan from Vietnam to investigate the situation and trade in copper and tin. The great geologist Le Gle led his students to visit here and wrote a book on the mineral resources of Yunnan. Later, he entered Yunnan from Vietnam via the Yunnan-Vietnam Railway and used this to also encroach on Guangxi and Guangdong provinces, which shows the danger of their intentions. The French coveted Yunnan for its benefits, and we have already known their unpredictable nature. However, the deep foresight of the British is more than that of the French. The author states in the book that the motive of the British covetousness of Yunnan can be summarized in one sentence: "Monopolizing the commerce of the Yangtze River." The various unequal treaties signed by the British and French with China and with Vietnam and Burma for use in Yunnan and Vietnam are also listed in detail to make it clear to the reader at a glance. This is truly a great work that deserves praise.

Therefore, the author's upper part is mainly a general description, summarizing the history of British and French imperialist aggression against Yunnan, and the various unequal treaties related to Yunnan signed with China, with concise explanations. The unique feature of this part is this, which deserves our attention.

Yunnan Province used to have Burma protecting it to the west and Vietnam protecting it to the south. Originally, it was a land of natural barriers. Since Burma was lost to Britain and Vietnam was annexed by France, the so-called defenses were completely removed, and it was surrounded by powerful neighbors, and border issues arose from this. In view of this, the author specifically and concisely describes the border affairs of Yunnan, Burma, and the northwest, and in the lower part, the author's description is mainly based on analysis and research. All Qing Dynasty's border disputes with Burma and issues related to the southwest border, such as the Pianma problem and the Jiangxinpo problem, are dissected in detail, which is not easily seen in other books, and its value can be known.

At the beginning of our country's construction, all our compatriots hope to pay attention to border issues. This is indeed a critical juncture for the enrichment and strength of our nation, but there are few specialized books that describe this issue from the correct standpoint on the market. This book is one of a series of border issues. The author's previous two books, "The Manchuria-Mongolia Problem" and "The Tibet Problem," are both important works. This newly published book, "The Yunnan Problem," can be used as a reference for our research. In the future, if the situation on the border can arouse the attention of the general public and thorough investigation, then we must praise the author of this book.

Page 23

Youth Garden

Random Notes from a Trip North

— Anping

8. Twelve Hours of Predestined Connection

Having written to this point, I cannot help but turn back and write about a very interesting incident I experienced in the train car.

The train seemed quite empty that day, and no other passenger ever entered my car. On the morning of the fourth, after the train had passed Xuzhou, I woke up and, in my hazy state, it seemed as if there was someone else in my No. 1 compartment. I opened my eyes slightly and saw a young woman standing at the foot of my bed, amusing a child with laughter. They were looking at the fields flying past the window, with their backs to me. I really felt a bit awkward at that moment. You might not believe me if I told you, but I am quite shy in many ways, like a virgin boy. I was afraid she would see me, so I quickly closed my eyes, kept still, and pretended to be still asleep. But my mind was racing with thoughts. I wondered how I could get up gracefully, maintain a Gentleman's demeanor, and not reveal any awkwardness. Think about it, how could an inexperienced young man bring himself to get dressed in front of a strange woman?

Thank goodness, she soon took the child and went to the corridor. I felt like a weight had been lifted off my chest and my heart stopped pounding. I gently closed the sliding door and then slowly got dressed.

The porter came to bring me washing water. After that, I went to the dining car for a light snack.

In the dining car, I had finished eating, and because it was comfortable sitting on the leather stools and looking at the scenery, and the dining car wasn't very busy at that time anyway, I sat there for a long time. But sooner or later I had to return to my compartment. Thinking that I had been sitting in the dining car for too long, which didn't seem right, I had to bite the bullet and walk back.

When I walked into my No. 1 compartment, she looked as if she was sitting on the bunk, bored. I, with the most appropriate posture and expression, smiled and nodded at her. She returned the greeting.

I said, "Going where?"

"Jinan."

"Got on at Xuzhou?"

"Yes."

At that moment, the child, who was kneeling on the bunk with his face pressed against the glass looking at the scenery, turned around and looked at me strangely. I smiled at him with the air of an adult. But, it would be more accurate to say that I smiled at the woman rather than at the child.

The woman spoke with a good Beijing accent, and seemed to be from a very respectable family. Although she was full of the kind of heroism that is unique to Northern women, that heroism also contained some of the charm of Southern beauties. She spoke politely, intelligently, and in a straightforward and direct manner, which is something that Northern women have that Southern women lack – a different kind of style. She was the first person to approach me, and she was also the first to give me a very beautiful impression.

That time, we talked a lot. Although we were excited, we couldn't help but think that it was just like two ships, occasionally brushing shoulders in the sea of people. On the same road, we would be separated in the blink of an eye, each going our own way, so there was no need to be so unrestrained. But, when the mood comes, there's nothing you can do. The woman was also very good at talking, as if she could talk to you about anything. Especially when she was talking about something, a small smile would occasionally bloom in her dimples, which was quite lovely.

The reason we talked so much that time was mostly due to her opening the conversation.

She asked, "What is your surname?"

"Chu," I said, "Chu as in Savings Bank."

"And your ancestral home?"

"Jiangsu... Yixing."

She thought for a moment, as if she was pondering something, and said, "Oh, are you from that XX aristocratic family?"

(I am ashamed to say that I have never been very clear about my family history. Someone asked me before if I was from the XX aristocratic family, and I was still confused and didn't dare to admit it. That person then asked if Chu Dawen was my ancestor. I said yes, but I don't know how many generations ago he was. He said, "Then that must be it." But I still couldn't remember clearly what kind of aristocratic family it was. I forgot. When she said this to me, it seemed to fit in my memory, so I said yes).

Unexpectedly, she said this, and at that time, my feeling was twofold: one was the patriarchal society's concept of family status, which gave me a sense of pride, and the other was how she knew about such things, which gave me a sense of surprise.

I began to develop a respectful attitude towards her. I learned a little about her background.

Her ancestral home was in a prefecture in Anhui, and her family was also a family of scholars for generations. She said that her family still had an extremely old couplet, which was written by someone from my ancestors. She was taught to read by her father from a young age. Her father was a remnant of the Qing Dynasty and had already passed away. She had also studied at a girls' middle school in Nanjing for two years.

This beginning, in fact, showed that she was an intellectual, which was the main reason why we were able to talk so much. However, although the conversation started with talking about family history, most of the topics of conversation still lingered on events after the May Fourth Movement.

We talked so well that day that she almost didn't bother to pay attention to her child. The child didn't understand what we were saying and often looked at me with his bright black eyes. I couldn't tell if there was welcome or hatred in his eyes, but he still spent most of his time looking at the scenery.

From Xuzhou to Jinan, it takes about twelve hours. Daybreak in Xuzhou, nightfall in Jinan, just a whole day. That day, I didn't notice whether time was passing quickly or slowly. I thought, spending a whole day lying on the bunk alone, relying on imagination to cope with loneliness, would be quite pitiful. Thank goodness, she came to brighten up my journey.

I often fixed my gaze on her face. To me, it really didn't mean anything, but it seemed that just looking at her face was enough to make me forget everything else. She wasn't a beauty, but just her two dimples were enough to make her attractive to look at. Yes, as soon as she showed a slight smile, I felt as happy as if I had drunk a glass of wine. I can still roughly remember how pretty her eyes were.

But focusing my gaze so intently on someone's face is impolite and undignified. However, sometimes when I wasn't looking at her, she seemed to be sneaking glances at me.

This situation was the most poetic and interesting, although it was a bit flirtatious.

Her figure was still completely that of a young woman. I don't think anyone would dare to guess that she was already eighteen years old. Looking at her, she should be at most seventeen years old. A mother with a child doesn't move people much, but an older sister with a younger sister or brother would evoke an unspeakable, indescribable feeling.

I thought the child should be her younger brother. She was very gentle and caring towards him, but I seemed to have heard the child call her "Mom" once. Could it be that she was really a "Mom"? I wished she was still a Miss.

Jinan had arrived. No force could stop her from getting off the train. A servant who had come with her in third class now hurried to second class to help her with her luggage. I saw her off with a very mysterious nod.

But in the end, I still didn't know her last name. Don't you think I'm muddleheaded?

Guidelines for Youth Section Submissions

(1) Articles should focus on discussions of youth issues, news from domestic and foreign schools or students, essays, descriptions of school life, etc., with no restrictions on style.

(2) Pictures should be limited to those related to youth issues.

(3) Photos should be qualified if they depict youth life (such as sports, travel, recreation, drama performances, gatherings, exhibitions, various competitions, etc.), school news, and youth movements. Individual photos and group photos are both welcome.

(4) Do not write on both sides of the manuscript paper.

(5) The number of words in each article should not exceed 2,000.
